Istihadah: Definition by Color and the Role of Habit
Defining istihadah by color with the habit exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istihadah in terms of color, apply the exception for habitual discharge, and distinguish when yellow/green/earthy discharge counts as hayd.

Core Idea
Yellow, green, or earthy discharge is istihadah unless it was the woman's habitual menstrual color before menopause.

This lesson focuses on the definition of istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding) as it relates to color and habit. The Hanafi school provides specific criteria for distinguishing istihadah from hayd based on the color of discharge and the woman's prior habit. Understanding this exception prevents incorrect application of menstrual rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of discharge that indicate istihadah
The passage lists yellow (sufrah), green (khudrah), and earthy (turabiyyah) as colors that default to istihadah.
These are non-red discharges usually not considered menstrual.
2
Understand the default ruling for menopausal women
For a woman who has reached the age of iyas (menopause), any such discharge after that age is istihadah.
The passage specifically mentions al-ayisah (menopausal woman).
3
Apply the exception for habitual discharge
If the woman had the same color discharge habitually before menopause, then it is considered menstruation, not istihadah.
Habit (al-'adah) overrides the default color ruling.
4
Derive the principle
The ruling illustrates the principle that habitual patterns (al-'adah) are taken into account in determining hayd.
This is a general fiqh principle: 'Custom is authoritative' (al-'adah muhakkamah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأقله ثلاثة أيام ولياليها ، وأكثره عشرة ، وعند أبي يوسف له أقله يومان ، وأكثر من اليوم الثالث ، وعند الشَّافِعِي له أقله يوم وليلة، وأكثره خمسة عشر ، ونحن نتمسك بقوله : أَقَلُّ الحَيْضِ لِلجَارِيَةِ البِكْرِ وَالتَّيْبِ ثَلاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيهَا ، وَأَكْثَرُهُ عَشْرَةُ أَيَّامٍ . واختار في «الهداية» بطلان العدة بالأشهر بعود الدم مطلقاً، وفي المسألة أقوال أخر مبسوم سوطة في «البحر». قوله : وإن رأت ; الآيسة بعد المدة المذكورة صُفرة بالضم بالفارسية : زردي ، أو خُضرة بالضم بالفارسية : سبنري، أو تُرَبيّة - بضم التاء المثناة الفوقية، وفتح الراء المهملة وكسر الباء الموحدة، وتشديد الياء المثناة التحتية : اللون الذي يشبه التراب ، فهي استحاضة، وهذا إذا لم تكن عادته كذلك، فإن كانت عادتها قبل الإياس الصفرة أو الخضرة أو التربية يكون ذلك حيضاً. كذا في «فتح القدير». قوله : بقوله... الخ؛ هذا الحديث أخرجه الطبراني من حديث أبي أمامة، والدارقطني من حديث واثلة ، وابن عدي من حديث معاذ ، وابن الجوزي من حديث أبي سعيد الخدري له ، وابن عدي من حديث أنس له وغيرهم
And its minimum is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten. And according to Abū Yūsuf, its minimum is two days and more than the third day, and according to al-Shāfiʿī, its minimum is a day and a night, and its maximum is fifteen. And we adhere to his statement: 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten days.' And he chose in 'al-Hidāyah' the invalidation of 'iddah by months with the return of blood absolutely, and there are other opinions in the matter detailed in 'al-Baḥr'. His statement: 'And if she sees' — meaning the menopausal woman after the mentioned duration — yellow (in Persian: zardī), or green (in Persian: sabzī), or earthy — with ḍammah on the tā', fatḥah on the rā', kasrah on the bā', and tashdīd on the yā': the color resembling earth — then it is istiḥāḍah. This is if that is not her habit; if her habit before menopause was yellow or green or earthy, then that is menstruation. As in 'Fatḥ al-Qadīr'. His statement: 'by his statement... etc.'; this ḥadīth was narrated by al-Ṭabarānī from Abū Umāmah, al-Dāraquṭnī from Wāthilah, Ibn ʿAdī from Muʿādh, Ibn al-Jawzī from Abū Saʿīd al-Khudrī, Ibn ʿAdī from Anas, and others.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah addresses foundational rulings on menstruation (ḥayḍ) and non-menstrual bleeding (istiḥāḍah). It begins by stating the minimum duration of menstruation: three complete days and nights, and the maximum: ten days. This is the established Hanafi position. The text then presents the opinions of Abū Yūsuf (minimum two days) and al-Shāfiʿī (minimum one day and night, maximum fifteen) to highlight the inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school relies on a ḥadīth of the Prophet (ṣallallāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam): 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten days.' This ḥadīth is cited as the proof (dalīl) for the Hanafi position. The commentary then mentions that al-Hidāyah chooses the absolute invalidation of 'iddah by months if blood returns, but does not elaborate further. Next, the definition of istiḥāḍah is given: if a woman (especially a menopausal woman) sees yellow, green, or earthy discharge after the age of īyās, it is istiḥāḍah, not menstruation. However, an important exception is noted: if such discharge was her habitual menstrual flow before menopause, then it is considered menstruation. This is based on the principle that habitual color and consistency are taken into account. The ḥadīth's chain of narration is also provided, indicating its authenticity according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الصفرة (al-ṣufrah): Yellow discharge; if habitual before menopause, it is considered menstrual; otherwise istiḥāḍah.
الخضرة (al-khuḍrah): Green discharge; same ruling as yellow.
الترابية (al-turābiyyah): Earthy-colored discharge; same ruling as yellow and green.
الآيسة (al-āyisah): A woman who has reached menopause (usually after 55 years of age in Hanafi fiqh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does yellow discharge count as menstruation (hayd) for a menopausal woman?
A) Always, because yellow is menstrual blood
B) Never, because menopausal women do not menstruate
C) Only if yellow was her habitual menstrual discharge before menopause
D) Only if the discharge lasts at least 3 days

Key Takeaway
Yellow, green, and earthy discharge are considered istihadah unless the woman had such discharge habitually before menopause, in which case it counts as menstruation.

The Duration of Menstruation: Minimum and Maximum
States Hanafi duration of hayd and disputes with Abu Yusuf and Shafi‘i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum and maximum duration of hayd, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, and cite the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
The minimum of hayd is three days and nights; the maximum is ten — fixed by hadith.

Menstruation (hayd) is a legal category that triggers specific prohibitions (prayer, fasting, marital relations). The Hanafi school defines its duration precisely based on transmitted texts. This lesson unpacks the authoritative Hanafi view, the dissenting opinions of Abu Yusuf (within the school) and Imam al-Shafi'i (outside it), and the proof that establishes the 3–10 day range.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
The text states the minimum is three days and nights and the maximum is ten days. Any bleeding outside this range is istihadha. Also, discharges of yellow, greenish, or dusty color are considered istihadha unless they occur during habit.
The ruling on colored discharge is a qualification: if such discharge appears habitually during menses, it counts as hayd.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that the minimum is two days and 'more than the third day' (i.e., just over two full days). The text does not mention Muhammad al-Shaybani's view here; the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's three full days.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf within the school, resolved by textual evidence.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i sets the minimum at one day and one night and the maximum at fifteen days. The Hanafi response is that a specific hadith restricts any general meaning and establishes the limits.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) affects whether a woman who bleeds for e.g., 2 days is considered in hayd or not.
4
Evaluate the proof
The Hanafi school adheres to a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ: 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten days.' This hadith, though transmitted through some weak chains, is accepted due to corroboration and the fatwas of the Sahaba.
The proof is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) that is qat'i in its indication for the Hanafis, as matters of quantity are not subject to analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة / الحيض وأقله ثلاثة أيام ولياليها وأكثره عشرة وإن رأت صُفْرَةً أو خُضْرَةً أو تُرْبِيَّةً فَهِيَ اسْتِحَاضَةٌ وأقله ثلاثة أيام ولياليها وأكثره عشرة وعند أبي يوسف له أقله يومان وأكثر من اليوم الثالث وعند الشَّافِعِي له أقله يوم وليلة وأكثره خمسة عشر ونحن نتمسك بقوله: أَقَلُّ الْحَيْضِ لِلْجَارِيَةِ الْبِكْرِ وَالثَّيِّبِ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيهَا وَأَكْثَرُهُ عَشَرَةُ أَيَّامٍ
Book of Purification / Menstruation: Its minimum is three days and their nights, its maximum is ten days. And if she sees yellow, or greenish, or dusty-colored [discharge], it is istihadha. Its minimum is three days and their nights, its maximum is ten days. According to Abu Yusuf, its minimum is two days and more than the third day. According to al-Shafi‘i, its minimum is a day and a night, and its maximum is fifteen. And we adhere to his statement: 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin girl and a non-virgin is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten days.'
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered dispute. First, the author states the Hanafi position: the minimum duration of hayd is three full days and nights (72 hours), and the maximum is ten days. Any blood beyond that is istihadha (non-menstrual bleeding). He then qualifies that colors like yellow (sufra), greenish (khudra), or dusty (turābiyya) are considered istihadha, but only if they are not habitual for the woman—if such discharge usually occurs during her menses, it counts as hayd. Next, the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf holds that the minimum is two days and less than three, i.e., just over two days. The text says 'more than the third day' which likely means the minimum is two days and a portion of the third. Then the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi‘i, who sets the minimum at one day and one night (24 hours) and the maximum at fifteen days. The author then presents the Hanafi proof: a hadith (though not fully quoted in the main text) attributed to the Prophet ﷺ stating the minimum of three days and maximum of ten. The footnote commentary (not included in this lesson's arabic_clean) explains that the hadith is transmitted through multiple weak chains but is accepted due to corroboration and fatwas of the Sahaba. This passage shows the Hanafi method of fixing legal quantities based on transmitted texts rather than mere analogy.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadha): Non-menstrual vaginal bleeding that occurs outside the normal days of hayd—either less than 3 days, more than 10 days, or beyond habit.
صُفْرَة (sufra): Yellowish discharge; in the context of hayd, it is considered istihadha unless it appears during a woman's habitual menses.
تُرْبِيَّة (turābiyya): Dust-colored (like earth) discharge; ruling same as sufra and khudra.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration of menstruation?
A) One day and one night
B) Two days
C) Three days and their nights
D) Ten days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes the minimum hayd at three days and nights and the maximum at ten days, relying on a specific hadith, and considers bleeding outside this range as istihadha, with Abu Yusuf and Shafi‘i holding differing views.

Defining the Start of Menses and Authenticating Its Hadith
Defines physical start of hayd and authenticates hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the start of menstruation according to the Hanafi school and explain the authentication of the hadith on its duration.

Core Idea
Menses begins only when blood reaches the outer vagina—internal flow does not count.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a critical boundary in Hanafi fiqh: when exactly does menstruation legally begin? The answer hinges on a physical definition that distinguishes the outer from the inner vagina. The author also addresses the authenticity of the hadith setting the minimum and maximum days, acknowledging its weak chains but arguing that multiple paths and Companion fatwas compensate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the term 'mabda' al-hayd' (start of menses) and note the key condition: blood must exit to the outer vagina (al-farj al-kharij).
2
Understand the analogy
The inner vagina is analogized to the mouth cavity, and the hymen to the teeth. Just as something hidden in the mouth is not considered 'out', so blood not reaching the outer vagina is not menses.
3
Examine the kursuf exception
If a kursuf (cotton/cloth) blocks blood from reaching the outer vagina, it is not considered menses until it appears externally.
This condition distinguishes hayd from istihadha.
4
Analyze hadith authentication
The hadith setting three days minimum and ten days maximum has weak chains, but the weakness is compensated (injabar) by multiple transmission paths and by fatwas of the Companions, which in matters not based on opinion have the ruling of marfu'.
This is the Hanafi justification for adopting the hadith.
5
State the Hanafi position
Therefore, the Hanafi school holds that the start of menses requires external appearance of blood, and the hadith on duration is authoritative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ اعلم أنَّ مبدأ الحيض من وقتِ خروج الدَّمِ إلى الفرج الخارج ووصول الدم إلى الفرج الداخل فإذا لم يصل إلى الفرج الخارج بحيلولة الكُرْسُف وفي أسانيدها ضعف كما بسطه الزَّيْلَعِي والعَيْنِي إلا أنه انجبر بكثرة الطريق وبفتاوى الصحابة
Then know that the beginning of menses is from the time the blood exits to the outer vagina and reaches the inner vagina. If it does not reach the outer vagina due to a barrier of kursuf (cotton/cloth). And in its chains [of transmission] there is weakness, as elaborated by al-Zayla‘i and al-‘Ayni, except that it is strengthened by the multiplicity of paths and by the fatwas of the Companions.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct legal points. First, it defines the physical start of menses (mabda' al-hayd): menstrual blood must exit the woman's body and reach the outer vagina (al-farj al-kharij). The inner vagina (al-farj al-dakhil) is analogized to the mouth cavity; the hymen is like teeth. Thus, if blood remains inside due to a plug of cotton (kursuf) and does not appear externally, it is not considered menstruation for legal purposes. The second point addresses the authenticity of the hadith cited earlier regarding the minimum and maximum of hayd. The author acknowledges that the hadith's chains contain weakness, but scholars like al-Zayla‘i and al-‘Ayni have examined them. The weakness is compensated (injarah) by the multiplicity of transmission paths (kathrat al-turuq) and by the fact that many Companions (Sahaba) gave fatwas in accordance with this hadith. These fatwas, since they concern matters not based on personal opinion (like defining durations), have the legal status of marfu‘ (attributed to the Prophet). Thus, the Hanafi position is firmly grounded in transmitted evidence.

Key Terms
مبدأ الحيض (mabda' al-hayd): The beginning of menstruation; defined as the moment when blood exits the uterus and reaches the external part of the vagina.
الفرج الخارج (al-farj al-kharij): The external part of the female genitalia, beyond the hymen; analogized to the lips of the mouth.
كُرْسُف (kursuf): A piece of cotton or cloth placed at the vaginal opening to absorb blood; if blood is blocked by it, it does not count as menses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the start of menstrual bleeding if the blood is blocked by a kursuf (cloth) and does not reach the outer vagina?
A) It is still considered menses because blood came out of the uterus.
B) It is not considered menses until it appears externally.
C) It is considered menses only if it exceeds three days.
D) It becomes istihadha immediately.

Key Takeaway
Menses legally begins only when blood reaches the outer vagina; the hadith on duration is accepted despite weak chains due to multiple supports.

Beginning of Menstruation: Blood Must Reach External Vagina
Defining hayd by blood exit to external vagina, with practical cotton pad test.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the start of menstruation and apply the cotton pad test to distinguish hayd from istihadah.

Core Idea
Menstruation begins only when blood exits the external vagina; internal bleeding does not break prayer.

This lesson defines the precise moment menstruation begins according to the Hanafi school. Using an anatomical analogy and the practical cotton pad test, the scholars clarify when a woman becomes impure (hayd) and must leave prayer. The ruling has significant daily application for women managing their religious duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key condition
The passage states that menstruation begins only when blood exits to the external vagina (al-farj al-kharij). Note the anatomical definition: the external vagina is the area from the labia to the hymen.
2
Understand the cotton pad test
A cotton pad (kursuf) is placed at the vaginal opening. The exit is determined by blood reaching the part of the pad adjacent to the external vagina. If blood only reaches the inner part (adjacent to internal vagina), exit is not realized until the pad is lifted.
3
Apply the ruling to prayer
If blood does not exit to the external part, the woman is not menstruating and must continue praying. She only leaves prayer when blood reaches the outer part of the pad.
4
Calculate the duration
Once the start is known (based on the cotton pad test), if the total bleeding period is 72 hours or more, it is hayd. If less, it is istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) and prayer is obligatory.
The fatwa is on the hour-counting method for leniency.
5
Recognize the proof
The minimum of three days (72 hours) is supported by fatwas of several Companions (Anas, Ibn Mas'ud, Mu'adh, etc.), which are treated as marfu' (elevated) because such quantities cannot be based on personal opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ اعلم أنَّ مبدأ الحيض من وقتِ خروج الدَّمِ إلى الفرج الخارج. قوله : إلى الفرج الخارج ؛ ذكر في «المحيط»: «أن ثقبة المرأة على صورة الفم ؛ فالفرج الداخل كمـا بين الأسنان وجوف الفم، وموضع البكارة كالأسنان، وهو حجاب رقيق يزولُ بالوطء وغيره، والفرج الخارج كما بين الشفتين والأسنان). قوله : بحيلولة الكرسف ؛ بضم الكاف والسين بينهما راء مهملة ساكنة، هو في الأصل القطن، وفي الاصطلاح عبارة عن قطعة قطن أو ثوب تضعه الحائض ونحوها على فم الفرج. فعند وضع الكُرْسفِ إنّما يتحقق الخروج إذا وصل الدم إلى ما يحاذي الفرج الخارج من الكُرْسف ، فإذا احمر من الكُرْسُف ما يحاذي الفرج الداخل لا يتحقق الخروج إلا إذا رفعت الكُرْسف، فيتحقق الخروج من وقتِ الرفع، وكذا في الاستحاضة، والنفاس، والبول. قوله : لا تقطع الصلاة ؛ أي لا تتركُ تلك المرأة الصلاة؛ لأنها ليست بحائضة لعدم خروج الدم إلى الفرج الخارج وإنما تترك الصلاة إذا وصل الدم إلى قطعة الكرسف المحاذية للفرج الخارج. قوله : من وقت الرفع ؛ أي رفع الكُرسف، يتفرّعُ عليه ما قال بعد سطور: فالطاهرة إذا وضعت الكُرسف في أوَّل الليل فحين أصبحت رأت عليه أثر الدم، فالآن يثبت حكم الحيض، والحائض إذا وضعت ورأت عليه البياض حين أصبحت حكم بطهارتها من حين وضعت. فإذا عُرف البداء والمنتهى ، فإن كان ما بينهما اثنتين وسبعين ساعة أو أكثر فالجميع حيض، وإن كان أقل فاستحاضة، وهذا أعني اعتبار الساعات اختيار أكثر المشايخ، ونقل عن الشيخ أبي اسحاق (له) أن هذا في أقل الحيض وأقل الطهر، وكان إذا أخبرته المرأة بالطهر في اليوم الحادي عشر أخذها بعشرة، وفي العاشر بتسعة، قال في «الكفاية» : «الفتوى على هذا تيسيرا». وفيه: فقد أخرج البيهقي والدارقطني عن أنس وابن مسعود ، والعقيلي عن معاذ ، والدارقطني عن عثمان ابن أبي العاص وغيرهم أنهم كانوا يفتون به، ومن المعلوم أن المقادير التي لا دخل فيها للرأي والاجتهاد الموقوف فيها كالمرفوع.
Then know that the beginning of menstruation is from the time blood exits to the external vagina. His statement: 'to the external vagina' is mentioned in al-Muhit: 'The woman's opening is shaped like a mouth; the internal vagina is like between the teeth and the interior of the mouth, the place of the hymen is like the teeth, a thin membrane that is removed by intercourse etc., and the external vagina is like between the lips and the teeth.' His statement: 'by the barrier of a cotton pad' — with damma on the kaf and sin, between them a silent ra, it originally means cotton, and technically is a piece of cotton or cloth that a menstruating woman etc. places on the mouth of the vagina. When a cotton pad is placed, the exit is only realized when blood reaches the part of the pad adjacent to the external vagina. If the part of the pad adjacent to the internal vagina becomes red, the exit is not realized unless the pad is lifted, so the exit is realized from the time of lifting. Likewise for istihadah, postpartum bleeding, and urine. His statement: 'it does not cut off prayer' means that woman does not leave prayer because she is not menstruating due to blood not exiting to the external vagina; she only leaves prayer when blood reaches the part of the pad adjacent to the external vagina. His statement: 'from the time of lifting' i.e., lifting the cotton pad. It follows from what he said later: The pure woman who places the pad at the beginning of the night and in the morning sees the trace of blood, then the ruling of menstruation is established from now. The menstruating woman who places it and sees whiteness in the morning is ruled pure from the time she placed it. If the beginning and end are known, then if what is between them is seventy-two hours or more, all is menstruation; if less, then istihadah. This consideration of hours is the choice of most mashayikh, and it is narrated from Sheikh Abu Ishaq that this is regarding the minimum of menstruation and minimum of purity. And if a woman informed him of purity on the eleventh day, he would take her as having ten days; on the tenth, nine. Al-Kifayah said: 'The fatwa is on this for leniency.' And in it: Al-Bayhaqi, al-Daraqutni reported from Anas, Ibn Mas'ud, al-'Uqayli from Mu'adh, al-Daraqutni from 'Uthman ibn Abi al-'As and others that they gave fatwa with it. And it is known that quantities in which there is no room for opinion and ijtihad, the mawquf is like marfu'.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof defining the start of menstruation in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that menstruation begins only when blood exits to the external vagina, not the internal. He clarifies the anatomy: the internal vagina is analogous to the area between the teeth and mouth interior, the hymen to the teeth (a thin membrane), and the external vagina to the lips and teeth. When a woman uses a cotton pad (kursuf), the exit is determined by whether blood reaches the part of the pad opposite the external vagina. If it only reaches the part opposite the internal vagina, it is not considered exit until the pad is lifted. This ruling applies equally to istihadah (non-cyclic bleeding), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and urine (for wudu nullification). Thus, if a woman sees blood only on the inner part of the pad, she does not leave prayer; she only leaves prayer when blood reaches the outer part. The practical application: a pure woman who inserts a pad at night and sees blood in the morning is considered menstruating from that morning. A menstruating woman who sees whiteness (purity) in the morning is considered pure from the time she inserted the pad (i.e., the previous night). For determining the duration of menstruation, the author adopts the method of most mashayikh: if the total time from start to end (based on the above criteria) is 72 hours or more, the entire period is menstruation; if less, it is istihadah. Sheikh Abu Ishaq had a stricter view: for minimums, he used a different calculation, but the fatwa is on the lenient hour-counting method. The proof for the three-day minimum is the fatwa of several Companions (Anas, Ibn Mas'ud, Mu'adh, 'Uthman ibn Abi al-'As), which is treated as marfu' (elevated) because such quantities are not based on personal opinion.

Key Terms
الفرج الخارج (al-farj al-kharij): The external part of the female genitalia, defined as the area from the lips (shafatayn) to the hymen (bikarah).
الكرسف (al-kursuf): A cotton or cloth pad placed on the vaginal opening to absorb blood; used to determine when blood has exited externally.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Non-menstrual uterine bleeding; distinguished from hayd and nifas by being less than three days or by other conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman places a cotton pad at Maghrib and sees blood on the inner part (adjacent to the internal vagina) at Fajr. According to the Hanafi school, when does she start leaving prayer?
A) From Maghrib, because blood has left the uterus.
B) From Fajr, because she saw blood that morning.
C) She does not leave prayer because the blood did not exit the external vagina.
D) She leaves prayer only if the blood reaches the outer part of the pad after lifting.

Key Takeaway
Menstruation begins when blood exits the external vagina; the cotton pad test verifies this, and a minimum of 72 hours is required for hayd; less is istihadah.

When Does a Menstruating Woman Stop Praying?
Defining the criterion for blood exiting the vagina for hayd rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for hayd to be established and apply the cotton test to determine when a woman must stop praying.

Core Idea
Hayd is only established when blood reaches the external vagina; internal discharge does not count.

This lesson clarifies a critical condition in the Hanafi school: a menstruating woman does not stop praying unless the blood actually exits to the external part of the vagina. Many assume any bleeding suffices, but the school requires external exit. We explore the use of a cotton test, the rules for istihadah and nifas, and the practical timing of 72 hours.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act in question is the woman's prayer. The default ruling is that she must continue praying unless a condition triggers its abandonment.
The matn says 'She does not leave the prayer' – meaning it remains obligatory.
2
Understand the condition for hayd
Hayd is established only when blood reaches the external vagina (al-farij al-kharij). Internal bleeding or staining on the inner part of the cotton does not count.
The cotton (kursuf) is placed to check: if the blood reaches the portion facing the external vagina, exit is realized.
3
Apply the cotton test
If a pure woman places cotton at night and sees blood on it in the morning, hayd is established from the time of placement. If a menstruating woman sees whiteness, purity is established from placement.
Exit is only confirmed when the cotton is lifted if the blood only reached the inner side.
4
Differentiate between hayd and istihadah using duration
If the known beginning and end of bleeding span 72 hours or more, all is hayd; if less, it is istihadah (irregular bleeding).
This 72-hour rule is the preferred view of most mashayikh for ease.
5
Extend the ruling to nifas and urine
The same external exit criterion applies to postpartum bleeding (nifas) and istihadah. For urine, wudu is not nullified until urine exits externally from the urethra.
Urine remaining in the bladder does not break wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة الحيض
لا تقطع الصلاة، فعند وضع الكرسف إنما يتحقق الخروج إذا وصل الدم إلى ما يحاذي الفرج الخارج من الكرسف، فإذا احمر من الكرسف ما يحاذي الفرج الداخل لا يتحقق الخروج إلا إذا رفعت الكرسف، فيتحقق الخروج من وقت الرفع، وكذا في الاستحاضة، والنفاس، والبول
[١]قوله : لا تقطع الصلاة ؛ أي لا تترك تلك المرأة الصلاة ؛ لأنها ليست بحائضة لعدم خروج الدم إلى الفرج الخارج وإنما تترك الصلاة إذا وصل الدم إلى قطعة الكرسف المحاذية للفرج الخارج. [٢] قوله : من وقت الرفع ؛ أي رفع الكرسف، يتفرع عليه ما قال بعد سطور: فالطاهرة إذا وضعت الكرسف في أول الليل فحين أصبحت رأت عليه أثر الدم، فالآن يثبت حكم الحيض، والحائض إذا وضعت ورأت عليه البياض حين أصبحت حكم بطهارتها من حين وضعت. فإذا عرف البداء والمنتهى ، فإن كان ما بينهما اثنتين وسبعين ساعة أو أكثر فالجميع حيض، وإن كان أقل فاستحاضة، وهذا أعني اعتبار الساعات اختيار أكثر المشايخ، ونقل عن الشيخ أبي اسحاق (۱) له أن هذا في أقل الحيض وأقل الطهر، وكان إذا أخبرته المرأة بالطهر في اليوم الحادي عشر أخذها بعشرة، وفي العاشر بتسعة، قال في «الكفاية» (۲) : «الفتوى على هذا تيسيرا». كذا في شرح مختصر الوقاية» للبرجندي. [٣]قوله : وكذا ؛ أي مثل الحكم المذكور في الاستحاضة والنفاس، فإذا خرج دم النفاس والاستحاضة إلى الخارج حكم بكونها مستحاضة وذات نفاس، وما لم يصل إلى الفرج الخارج لا يحكم به. [٤] قوله : والبول ؛ يعني يعتبر خروجه إلى الخارج لا زواله عن موضعه، فما دام في المثانة ولم يخرج من رأس الذكر لا ينتقض الوضوء.
The Book of Purification: Menstruation. She does not leave the prayer. For when placing the cotton, indeed exiting is realized only if the blood reaches the part of the cotton facing the external vagina. If the part of the cotton facing the internal vagina becomes red, exiting is not realized unless she lifts the cotton, so exiting is realized from the time of lifting. Similarly for istihadah, nifas, and urine. [1] His saying: 'She does not leave the prayer'; meaning that woman does not leave the prayer because she is not menstruating due to the blood not exiting to the external vagina. She only leaves the prayer if the blood reaches the piece of cotton facing the external vagina. [2] His saying: 'From the time of lifting'; meaning lifting the cotton. This gives rise to what he said later: So a pure woman if she places the cotton at the beginning of the night and in the morning sees a trace of blood on it, then now the ruling of menstruation is established. And a menstruating woman if she places the cotton and in the morning sees whiteness on it, she is ruled to be pure from the time she placed it. So if the beginning and end are known, then if between them is seventy-two hours or more, all of it is menstruation; if less, then istihadah. This considering hours is the choice of most mashayikh. It is narrated from Abu Ishaq that this is regarding the minimum of menstruation and minimum of purity. He used to, if a woman informed him of purity on the eleventh day, take her as having it for ten days; on the tenth, nine. Al-Kifayah said: 'The fatwa is on this for ease.' Similarly in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah al-Birjandi. [3] His saying: 'Similarly'; meaning like the mentioned ruling in istihadah and nifas. So if blood of nifas and istihadah exits to the outside, she is ruled to be a mustahadah or one with nifas; if it does not reach the external vagina, it is not ruled. [4] His saying: 'and urine'; meaning its exit to the outside is considered, not its leaving its place. So as long as it is in the bladder and has not exited from the head of the penis, wudu is not nullified.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling that a menstruating woman does not stop praying unless the blood actually exits to the external part of the vagina. The commentator explains that the criterion is the blood reaching the portion of the cotton that corresponds to the external vagina. If the blood only reaches the internal part, it is not considered exiting until the cotton is lifted. This ruling also applies to istihadah (irregular bleeding) and nifas (postpartum bleeding). For urine, wudu is not nullified until it exits externally. The commentator also discusses the practical application: if a pure woman places cotton at night and sees blood in the morning, hayd is established from the time of placement; if a menstruating woman sees whiteness, purity is established from placement. The minimum duration for hayd is discussed: if the total time of bleeding is 72 hours or more, it is hayd; otherwise, istihadah. This view is attributed to most mashayikh and adopted for fatwa for ease.

Key Terms
الكُرْسُف (al-kursuf): A piece of cotton placed by a woman to check for menstrual bleeding.
الفرج الخارج (al-farij al-kharij): The external part of the vagina visible from outside.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular vaginal bleeding that is not menstrual or postpartum.

Key Takeaway
A woman does not leave prayer unless blood exits to the external vagina; internal bleeding is not hayd.

Ruling on Urine Reaching the Prepuce (Wudu Nullification)
Stating the ruling that the prepuce is considered external for wudu nullification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the prepuce is considered external for wudu nullification and apply it to an uncircumcised man's case.

Core Idea
The prepuce is legally external; urine reaching it nullifies wudu even without visible exit.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling in taharah for uncircumcised men. The Hanafi school holds that the prepuce (qulfa) is treated as part of the external body in the context of wudu nullification. Therefore, if urine reaches the prepuce, wudu is nullified even if the urine does not exit. This distinction is based on a detailed principle discussed earlier in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and event
The ruling applies to an uncircumcised man whose urine leaves the bladder and reaches the prepuce.
The prepuce is the skin that would be removed during circumcision.
2
Understand the legal equivalence
The text states that the prepuce is like the exterior (khal-kharji) in all respects regarding wudu nullification.
This is the key principle: the prepuce is not considered internal.
3
Apply the ruling
Once urine reaches the prepuce, wudu is nullified regardless of whether it appears externally.
Renewal of wudu becomes wajib.
4
Differentiate from common assumption
Many assume that only actual exit of urine nullifies wudu. For uncircumcised men, the criterion is reaching the prepuce, not exit.
This is a critical refinement of the general rule.

[ 1 ] قوله والقلفة ; يعني إذا خرج بولُ مَن لم يختن من المثانة ووصل إلى القلفة وهو بالضم : الجلد الذي يقطع عند الختان، ولم يظهر خارجاً منها يحكم بانتقاض الوضوء ; لأنَّ حكم القلفة حكم الخارج من كلِّ وجه في باب انتقاض الوضوء، كما مر تفصيله في «بحث فرائض الغسل».

[1] His saying: 'and the prepuce'; meaning if urine of one who is not circumcised exits from the bladder and reaches the prepuce – and it (with damm) is the skin that is cut during circumcision – and does not appear outside of it, it is ruled that wudu is nullified, because the ruling of the prepuce is like the ruling of the exterior in every respect in the chapter of nullification of wudu, as detailed previously in 'Research on Obligatory Acts of Ghusl'.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding wudu nullification for uncircumcised men. The author states that if a man places cotton in his urethra (to check for urine), the prepuce is treated as external. The commentator explains that this means if urine reaches the prepuce (the skin that would be removed during circumcision) but does not emerge from it, wudu is nevertheless nullified because the prepuce is legally considered exterior. This is based on the principle that the prepuce is like the external part of the penis in the context of ritual impurity. The ruling is specific to uncircumcised men and is an established part of the Hanafi school's teachings on wudu nullification.

Key Terms
الْقُلْفَة (al-qulfa): The prepuce, the fold of skin covering the glans of an uncircumcised penis.
انْتِقَاض الْوُضُوء (intiqad al-wudu): Nullification of wudu; requiring renewal for prayer.

Placing Cotton for Menstrual Check
Clarifying the ruling on placing cotton for checking hayd and purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on placing cotton for menstrual checking for a virgin and a thayyib, and explain the Hanafi position on the timing of purity and menstruation based on the color seen on the cotton.

Core Idea
Placing cotton is recommended for a thayyib always, but for a virgin only during menses, due to her ability to feel the flow.

This lesson examines a detailed ruling from the Hanafi tradition regarding the placement of cotton (kursuf) to check for menstrual bleeding and purity. The text distinguishes between a virgin (bikr) and a non-virgin (thayyib), and provides practical guidance on when a woman is considered menstruating or pure based on what she sees on the cotton. Understanding this ruling helps women correctly determine their state of purity for prayer and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Placing cotton (wuḍʿ al-kursuf) for checking menstrual bleeding. The base ruling: mustahabb (recommended) for a virgin during menses, and for a thayyib in every situation.
The commentator upgrades this to sunnah during menses for both.
2
Understand the distinction between bikr and thayyib
Why the difference? A thayyib has a wider vaginal opening, so blood may flow without her feeling it. Therefore, she is advised to place cotton even during purity to detect any unexpected blood. A virgin can usually feel the flow, so placement during purity is not recommended.
This is a precautionary measure (iḥtiyāṭ) for the thayyib.
3
Learn the correct placement and its prohibition
The cotton should be placed at the 'place of virginity' (mawḍiʿ al-bakārah), which is between the external and internal vagina. Placing it inside the vagina (al-farj al-dākhil) is disliked (makrūh).
Internal placement is discouraged due to potential harm.
4
Determine the ruling when seeing blood or whiteness
If a pure woman places cotton at night and sees a trace of blood in the morning, she is considered menstruating from that time. If a menstruating woman sees whiteness (clear discharge) on the cotton, she becomes pure from the time she placed it.
The white discharge is called al-qissaḥ al-bayḍā and is a sign of purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[٤] قوله : ورأت عليه البياض ; والمراد به إمّا بياض الثوب، والمقصود أنها رأته صافياً غير ملون بشيء، وإما شيءٌ يخرج من أقبال النساء بعد انقطاع الدم شبيهاً بالخيط الأبيض.

Then placing the cotton is recommended for a virgin during menses, and for a thayyib (woman who has had intercourse) in every situation. Its place is the place of virginity, and it is disliked in the internal vagina. So a pure woman if she places it at the beginning of the night and in the morning sees a trace of blood on it, then the ruling of menstruation is established now. A menstruating woman if she places it at the beginning of the night and in the morning sees whiteness on it, she is ruled to be pure from the time she placed it. [2] His saying: 'recommended for a virgin during menses'; rather it is sunnah for both virgin and thayyib during menses, due to the hadith reported about it, and it is known from the practices of the wives of the Companions and others. The difference between virgin and thayyib is in the recommendation of placing cotton for the thayyib during purity as well, not for the virgin. The reason is that with the loss of virginity there is increased width in her vagina, and her blood descends more quickly and is seldom felt, so it is better to place cotton in every situation as a precaution, not so for the virgin. [3] His saying: 'place of virginity'; which is between the external and internal vagina. This is what is meant by the hadith narrated by Malik and others: 'Women used to send to Aisha a cloth with cotton containing yellowness from menstrual blood asking her about prayer, and she would say to them: Do not rush until you see the white discharge, meaning thereby purity from menses.'

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on placing cotton (kursuf) to check for menstrual bleeding. The author states it is recommended (mustahabb) for a virgin during menstruation and for a thayyib (non-virgin) in all states. The commentator upgrades this to sunnah for both during menses, citing a hadith. The difference is that for a thayyib, it is also recommended during purity because her vaginal opening is wider and blood may descend without her feeling it. Placement should be at the 'place of virginity' (between external and internal vagina); internal placement is disliked. Practical application: if a pure woman places cotton at night and sees blood in the morning, hayd is established from that time. If a menstruating woman sees whiteness (clear discharge indicating purity), she becomes pure from the time of placement. The whiteness is either the white of the cloth or the white discharge (qissah bayda) mentioned in a hadith from Aisha.

Key Terms
الْبِكْر (al-bikr): A virgin woman who has not had intercourse.
الثَّيِّب (al-thayyib): A woman who has had intercourse (non-virgin).
الْقَصَّة الْبَيْضَاء (al-qissah al-bayda): A white discharge indicating the end of menstruation and purity.
الْكُرْسُف (al-kursuf): A piece of cotton used to check menstrual bleeding.

A) Inside the vagina

Key Takeaway
Placing cotton to check hayd is recommended (mustahabb/sunnah) and its correct placement is at the exit, not inside; the distinction between virgin and thayyib is based on the woman's ability to feel the flow.

Placing Cotton and Signs of Menstruation and Purity
Ruling on placing cotton and signs of menstruation and purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing cotton for a virgin and non-virgin during menstruation and purity, and apply the signs to determine the beginning and end of menstruation.

Core Idea
Seeing blood starts menstruation; seeing clear whiteness ends it, retroactive to the placement time.

A key practical issue for women in taharah is knowing when menstruation begins and ends. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the use of cotton (kursuf) to detect blood and whiteness, and the rulings that follow. We will unpack the conditions, the distinction between virgin and non-virgin, and the hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for virgins and non-virgins
The passage states that placing cotton is mustahabb (recommended) for a virgin during menstruation, and for a non-virgin in all states (menstruation and purity). The commentator upgrades it to sunnah during menstruation for both based on hadith. Note the difference: for non-virgins, it is also recommended during purity due to extra precaution.
The ruling for non-virgins is continuous; for virgins only during menses.
2
Determine the correct placement and what is disliked
The place of placement is the 'place of the hymen' (between outer and inner vagina). It is makruh (disliked) to place it inside the inner vagina. This ensures the cotton checks the vaginal opening without harm.
Proper placement is crucial for accurate detection.
3
Apply the sign for the beginning of menstruation
If a pure woman places cotton at night and in the morning sees a trace of blood, the ruling of menstruation is established from the time she placed the cotton. This means her menstrual period begins retroactively.
This applies to a woman who was pure before.
4
Apply the sign for the end of menstruation (purity)
If a menstruating woman places cotton at night and in the morning sees whiteness (clear discharge), she is ruled pure from the time she placed the cotton. The whiteness is the sign of purity, as confirmed by the hadith of Aisha.
Purity is retroactive to the placement time, allowing her to consider missed acts during that period.
5
Examine the hadith evidence and its legal implication
The passage cites the hadith where Aisha told women not to hasten to pray until they see the white discharge. This proves that whiteness is the definitive sign of purity, and its ruling is derived from the command 'do not hasten'.
The hadith is from Muwatta, Bukhari, and Muslim, all ahad but sufficient for this ruling.

ووضعُ الرَّجلِ القُطْنةَ في الإحليل، والقُلفة كالخارج. ثمَّ وَضَعُ الكُرْسُفِ مُسْتَحَبُّ للبكر في الحيض، وللثيب في كل حال، وموضعه موضع البكارة " ، ويُكْرَهُ في الفرج الداخل ، فالطَّاهِرةُ إِذا وَضَعَت أَوَّل الليل، فحين أصبحت رأت عليه أثر الدم، فالآن يثبت حكم الحيض، والحائض إذا وَضَعَتْ أول الليل ورأت عليه البياض حين أصبحت حكم بطهارتها من حين وَضَعَتْ.
[ 1 ] قوله والقلفة ؛ يعني إذا خرج بولُ مَن لم يختن من المثانة ووصل إلى القلفة وهو بالضم : الجلد الذي يقطع عند الختان، ولم يظهر خارجاً منها يحكم بانتقاض الوضوء ؛ لأنَّ حكم القلفة حكم الخارج من كلِّ وجه في باب انتقاض الوضوء، كما مر تفصيله في «بحث فرائض الغُسل».
[٢]قوله : مستحب للبكر في الحيض ؛ بل سنة للبكر والثيب كليهما حالة الحيض ، بذلك ورد الحديث (۱) ، وهو المعلوم من أحوال نساء الصحابة وغيرهم. والفرق بين البكر والثيب في استحباب وضع الكرسف للثيب حالة الطهر أيضاً دون البكر، ووجهه : أنَّ بزوال البكارة يكون في فرجها سعة زائدة، ويكون نزول دمها أسرع ، وقَلْما يُحَس به، فالأولى هو وضع الكُرسف في كلِّ حال احتياطاً ولا كذلك
(۳) قوله : موضع البكارة ؛ وهو ما بين الفرج الخارج والداخل.
[٤] قوله : ورأت عليه البياض ؛ والمراد به إمّا بياض الثوب، والمقصود أنها رأته صافياً غير ملون بشيء، وإما شيءٌ يخرج من أقبال النساء بعد انقطاع الدم شبيهاً بالخيط الأبيض.
وهو المراد من حديث رواه مالك وغيره : «كان النساء يبعثن إلى عائشة بالدرجة
(۱) منها عن أم علقمة مولاة عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها قالت: كان النساء يبعثن إلى عائشة أم المؤمنين بالدرجة فيها الكرسف فيه الصفرة من دم الحيضة يسألنها عن الصلاة فتقول لهن : لا تعجلن حتى ترين القصة البيضاء تريد بذلك الطهر من الحيضة في «الموطأ» (۱ : ٥٩)، و صحيح البخاري (۱) : (۱۲۱)، و«صحیح مسلم» (٢ : ٦٥٠)، وغيرها.
And the man's placing of the cotton in the urethra, and the foreskin is like the outside. Then, placing the cotton is recommended for a virgin during menstruation, and for a non-virgin in every condition, and its place is the place of the hymen, and it is disliked inside the inner vagina. So a pure woman, if she places it at the beginning of the night, and in the morning she sees on it a trace of blood, then the ruling of menstruation is established. And a menstruating woman, if she places it at the beginning of the night and sees on it whiteness in the morning, her purity is ruled from the time she placed it. [1] His saying: 'and the foreskin' means that if the urine of an uncircumcised man exits the bladder and reaches the foreskin—and it is, with damma, the skin that is cut during circumcision—and it does not appear outside it, the wudu is ruled to be broken, because the ruling of the foreskin is the ruling of the outside in every respect in the chapter of breaking wudu, as detailed previously in the discussion of the obligations of ghusl. [2] His saying: 'recommended for a virgin during menstruation' rather it is sunnah for both a virgin and a non-virgin during menstruation; the hadith (1) has been reported to that effect, and it is known from the condition of the wives of the Companions and others. And the difference between a virgin and a non-virgin in the recommendation of placing cotton for the non-virgin also in the state of purity, not for the virgin, and its reason is that with the loss of virginity there is extra capacity in her vagina, and her blood descends faster, and it is rarely felt, so it is better to place cotton in every condition as a precaution, and not similarly. (3) His saying: 'the place of the hymen' and it is what is between the outer and inner vagina. [4] His saying: 'and she saw whiteness on it' and what is meant by it is either the whiteness of the cloth, and the intent is that she saw it clear, not colored by anything, or something that exits from the front parts of women after the cessation of blood, resembling a white thread. And that is what is meant by the hadith narrated by Malik and others: 'The women used to send to Aisha the tray (1) from her, from Umm Alqama, the freed slave of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, that she said: The women used to send to Aisha, the Mother of the Believers, the tray containing cotton with yellowness from menstrual blood, asking her about prayer, and she would say to them: Do not hasten until you see the white discharge, meaning thereby purity from menstruation.' In al-Muwatta (1:59), and Sahih al-Bukhari (1:121), and Sahih Muslim (2:650), and others.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the use of cotton (kursuf) by women to determine the beginning and end of menstruation. The passage begins by establishing that placing cotton in the urethra or on the foreskin has implications for wudu (the foreskin is treated as external, so if urine reaches it, wudu is broken). Then it addresses women: placing cotton is recommended (mustahabb) for a virgin during menstruation and for a non-virgin (thayyib) in all states, both menstruation and purity. The commentator clarifies that it is actually sunnah for both types during menstruation, based on a hadith. The place of placement is the position of the hymen, between the outer and inner vagina, and it is disliked (makruh) to place it inside the inner vagina. The ruling then explains how to determine the onset of menstruation: if a pure woman places cotton at night and sees blood in the morning, menstruation begins from that time. Similarly, if a menstruating woman places cotton and sees whiteness (bayad) in the morning, she becomes pure from that time. The commentator explains that 'whiteness' refers to a clear, colorless discharge or a white thread-like substance, which is the sign of purity, as narrated in the hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) where she advised women to wait until they see the white discharge before praying. This hadith is found in the Muwatta, Bukhari, and Muslim. The passage also notes that for a non-virgin, it is recommended to use cotton even during purity due to the increased likelihood of unseen blood flow.

Key Terms
كرسف (kursuf): Cotton or cloth placed by a woman at the vaginal opening to check for blood or discharge.
قلفة (qulfah): The foreskin of the penis; in this context, it is treated as external for wudu purposes.
بياض (bayad): The white discharge or clear fluid that signals the end of menstruation.
بكارة (bakarah): Virginity; the state of being a virgin. The 'place of the hymen' is the area between the outer and inner vagina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a menstruating woman become pure if she places cotton at night and sees whiteness in the morning?
A) From the time she placed the cotton
B) From the time she saw the whiteness
C) From the morning prayer time
D) At noon of that day

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the placement of cotton to objectively determine menstruation and purity, with clear signs: blood for onset, whiteness for end, and purity ruled retroactively.

Intervening Purity Between Menstrual Bleedings: The Hanafi Ruling and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Defines intervening purity and its ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid intervening purity, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a purity of 3-14 days separates two menstrual periods.

Core Idea
A purity less than 15 days does not separate two menstrual periods in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Correctly classifying menstrual blood is essential for determining a woman's prayer, fasting, and other worship obligations. The text defines 'intervening purity' (al-tuhr al-mutakhallal) and its two categories: valid (sahih) and invalid (fasid). It then presents a key intra-Hanafi difference: if a woman sees a break in bleeding lasting 3 days or more but less than 15, does that break separate the bleedings into two distinct menstrual periods, or does the entire interval count as continuous menstruation? The answer has direct practical consequences for a woman's religious duties.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
First, understand the key terms: al-tuhr al-mutakhallal (intervening purity), al-tuhr al-sahih (valid purity = 15+ days), al-tuhr al-fasid (invalid purity = less than 15 days), and al-fasl (separation). The minimum valid purity is 15 days by agreement.
2
Identify the consensus zone
If the intervening purity is less than 3 days, there is consensus that it does not separate the bleedings; the entire duration is treated as continuous menstruation. This is the first clear ruling.
3
Locate the point of ikhtilaf
When the intervening purity is between 3 and 14 days (i.e., at least 3 days but less than 15), the Hanafi masters differed. The earlier opinion of Abu Hanifa held that such a purity does separate, while Abu Yusuf and the later opinion of Abu Hanifa held that it does not.
4
Apply the tarjih (preference)
The commentator states 'وعليه الفتوى' (the fatwa is upon it) for the opinion that it does not separate. This is the mufta bihi position for the school. Understand the reasoning: since the minimum valid purity is 15 days, anything less is 'fasid' and thus cannot achieve 'fasl'.
5
Extend to nifas (postpartum bleeding)
The text also notes the ruling for nifas within 40 days: Abu Hanifa holds that no intervening purity separates, regardless of length; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say a 15-day purity does separate. The fatwa follows Abu Hanifa.

[٢] قوله: أي بين الدمين؛ لم يقل: بين الحيضين؛ لأنه لا يلزم أن يكون الدم المحيط بالطرفين حيضاً كما سيذكره مفصلاً. [٣] قوله: في مدته؛ قال الشارح الهروي هو حال من الدمين المذكورين ضمناً، وكونهما في مدة الحيض يستلزم كونَ الطهر المحاط بهما أيضاً كذلك، ولو جعل من الضمير في المتخلّل أو من التخلّل المذكور حكماً لا يظهر المقصود؛ إذ لا يلزمُ من كون الطهر بين الدمين أو كون تخلّله بينهما في مدة الحيض كونهما في مدة الحيض. [0] قوله: وما رأت؛ أي ولفظ ما رأت عطف عليه: أي على الطهر، وهو مصدر بمعنى المفعول - أي معطوف - أو صيغة مجهول ماض، أو صيغة معروف وضميره يرجع إلى ما يرجع إليه ضمير قوله: «فقوله»، وهو المصنف له المذكور حكماً. واعلم أنَّ الطَّهِّرَ الذي يكون أقل من خمسة عشر إذا تخلل بين الدمين: فإن كان أقل من ثلاثة أيام لا يفصل بينهما، بل هو كالدم المتوالي إجماعاً. وإن كان ثلاثة أيام أو أكثر، فعند أبي يوسف وهو قول أبي حنيفة آخراً لا يفصل، وإن كان أكثر ) [1] قوله: واعلم؛ الغرض منه تفصيل المذاهب الواقعة في الطهر الفاسد المتخلل. [٢] قوله: الذي يكون أقل؛ قيد به لأنه إن كان المتخلّل بين الدمين مقدار خمسة عشر يوماً، كان فاصلاً اتفاقاً لا حيضاً، مثل أن ترى المرأة ثلاثة دماً ثم خمسة عشر طهراً، ثم ثلاثة دماً. [٣] قوله: فإن كان؛ أي ذلك المتخلل أقل من ثلاثة أيام، نحو أن ترى يوماً دماً، ثم يومين طهراً، ثم يومين دماً. [٤] قوله: لا يفصل؛ الفصل عبارة عن كونه طهراً صحيحاً، وعدم الفصل عبارة عن أن لا يجعل الطهر طهراً، بل يجعل كأيام ترى فيها الدم. [٥] قوله: ثلاثة أيام؛ نحو أن ترى يومين دماً، وثلاثة طهراً، ثمّ في اليوم السادس دماً. [٦] قوله: أو أكثر؛ أي من ثلاثة أيام، وإن كان أكثر من عشرة أيام كأن ترى امرأة دماً يوماً، وعشرة أيام طهراً، ثم يوماً دماً، كذا أفاده الوالد العلام في رسالته: «التعليق الفاصل في مسألة الطهر المتخلل»، وما في: التعليق الكامل في مسألة الطهر المتخلل» لبعض معاصريه: أو أكثر من ثلاثة أيام إلى عشرة. انتهى. فليس بصحيح. [٧] قوله: لا يفصل؛ أي لا يكون الطهر الذي هو ثلاثة أيام أو أكثر منه، كان أكثر من عشرة أيام طهراً، بل يجعل كأيَّامٍ متوالية للدم، وذلك لأنَّ مدَّةَ الطهرِ الصحيح الفاصل خمسة عشر يوماً وما دونه فاسد، فلا يجري عليه حكم الصحيح، وهو الفصل للمنافاة البينة بين الصحة والفساد. [۸] قوله: أكثر؛ لكن بشرط أن يكون أقل من خمسة عشر يوماً، ولو نصف اليوم أو أقل، وإنما لم يذكره؛ لأنَّه فَهِمَ من السابق، فإنَّ الكلام إنَّما هو من الطهر الفاسد. (1) لأن أقل مدة بين الحيضتين خمسة عشر يوماً ولياليها بالاتفاق.
The intervening purity within its duration, and whatever color she sees in it besides pure white is menstruation. His statement: 'al-tuhr' (purity) is used in the terminology of jurists to mean the time period separating two bleedings, its minimum is fifteen days, and its maximum has no limit. If it amounts to fifteen days, it is a valid purity upon which the rulings of purification from menstruation apply, and if it is less than that, it is invalid. [2] His statement: 'between the two bleedings'; he did not say 'between the two menstruations' because it is not necessary that the blood surrounding the two ends be menstruation, as he will detail. [3] His statement: 'in its duration'; the Harawi commentator said it is a circumstantial accusative from the two bleedings mentioned implicitly, and their being in the menstrual period necessitates the purity surrounding them also being likewise. If it were made from the pronoun in 'al-mutakhallal' or from the stated 'takhallul' as a ruling, the intended meaning would not appear; for it does not follow from the purity being between two bleedings or its interposition between them within the menstrual period that the two bleedings are within the menstrual period. [4] His statement: 'menstruation ... etc.'; meaning in reality or in ruling. And the intervening purity between two bleedings in postpartum bleeding (nifas) within forty days does not separate according to Abu Hanifa, whether it is fifteen days or less or more, and the surrounding of blood at both ends is considered like continuous blood, and the fatwa is upon it. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the fifteen days do separate. As in 'al-Tatarkhaniyya'. [0] His statement: 'and whatever she sees'; meaning the phrase 'ma ra'at' is conjoined to it, i.e., to 'al-tuhr', and it is a verbal noun in the sense of the object – i.e., conjoined – or a form of the passive past, or a form of the active past and its pronoun refers to what the pronoun of his statement 'fa-qawluhu' refers to, which is the author implied as a ruling. Know that the purity that is less than fifteen days, if it intervenes between two bleedings: if it is less than three days, it does not separate between them, rather it is like continuous blood by consensus. And if it is three days or more, then according to Abu Yusuf and it is the latter opinion of Abu Hanifa, it does not separate, even if it is more. [1] His statement: 'know'; its purpose is detailing the legal positions occurring regarding the invalid intervening purity. [2] His statement: 'which is less'; he restricted it because if the intervening between the two bleedings amounts to fifteen days, it separates by agreement and is not menstruation, such as a woman seeing blood for three days then purity for fifteen days then blood for three days. [3] His statement: 'if it is'; meaning that intervening is less than three days, such as she sees blood one day, then purity two days, then blood two days. [4] His statement: 'does not separate'; separation (fasl) means it is a valid purity, and lack of separation means the purity is not made purity but rather made like days in which she sees blood. [5] His statement: 'three days'; such as she sees blood two days, and purity three days, then on the sixth day blood. [6] His statement: 'or more'; meaning more than three days, even if more than ten days, such as a woman seeing blood one day, and purity ten days, then blood one day. So stated the noble father in his treatise 'al-Ta'liq al-Fasil fi Mas'alat al-Tuhr al-Mutakhallal', and what is in 'al-Ta'liq al-Kamil fi Mas'alat al-Tuhr al-Mutakhallal' by some of his contemporaries: or more than three days up to ten. End. So it is not correct. [7] His statement: 'does not separate'; meaning that the purity which is three days or more, even if more than ten days, is not considered purity, rather it is made like consecutive days of blood, because the duration of valid separating purity is fifteen days and what is less than it is invalid, so the ruling of the valid does not apply to it, which is separation, due to the clear contradiction between validity and invalidity. [8] His statement: 'more'; but with the condition that it be less than fifteen days, even half a day or less, and he did not mention it because he understood from the preceding, since the discussion is only about invalid purity. (1) Because the minimum period between two menstruations is fifteen days and their nights by agreement.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal status of the intervening purity (tuhr) between two episodes of menstrual blood. The matn initially defines that any color seen during the menstrual period except pure white is considered menstrual blood. The commentator then focuses on the intervening purity (al-tuhr al-mutakhallal) between two bleedings. The key ruling is that a valid separating purity must be at least fifteen days; anything less is invalid (fasad). Within invalid purity, there is a further division: if the intervening period is less than three days, it does not separate at all by consensus; it is treated as continuous blood. If it is three days or more (but less than fifteen), Abu Yusuf and the latter opinion of Abu Hanifa hold that it still does not separate, meaning the entire duration is considered a single continuous menstrual period. The earlier opinion of Abu Hanifa (and possibly Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that a three-day or more purity does separate, but the commentator states that the fatwa is on the position of non-separation. The passage then clarifies that this discussion applies only when the purity is less than fifteen days; if it is exactly fifteen or more, it is a valid separating purity by agreement. The commentary also mentions that for postpartum bleeding (nifas), the same rule applies: Abu Hanifa does not consider any intervening purity within the forty days as separating, while the Sahibayn consider a fifteen-day interval as separating. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the latter opinion.

Key Terms
الطهر المتخلل (al-tuhr al-mutakhallal): The period of purity that occurs between two episodes of bleeding
الطهر الصحيح (al-tuhr al-sahih): A valid purity that is at least 15 days long
الطهر الفاسد (al-tuhr al-fasid): A purity less than 15 days that is treated as part of the menstrual period
الفصل (al-fasl): The legal effect of a purity being valid, meaning it separates two menstrual periods

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling if a woman sees blood for 2 days, then a purity of 5 days, then blood again?
A) The 5-day purity separates the two bleedings, making them two separate menstrual periods.
B) The entire 2+5+2 days are considered one continuous menstrual period, and she must not pray.
C) She should wait until she sees the white discharge to determine if the purity is valid.
D) The 5-day purity is valid only if it occurs within the 10-day maximum menstruation.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, only a purity of 15 full days separates two menstrual periods; anything less is treated as continuous menstruation.

The Ruling on Intervening Purity Between Bleedings
Explains the Hanafi ruling on intervening purity less than 15 days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an intervening purity of less than 15 days and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A purity less than 15 days never separates two bleedings in the Hanafi school, even if it is three or more days.

The question of whether a short period of cleanliness between two episodes of bleeding constitutes a new menstrual cycle is crucial for determining a woman's obligations in prayer and fasting. In this passage, the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the Hanafi position and resolves an intra-school dispute. The key principle: any intervening purity that is less than the minimum interval of 15 days is legally invalid (fasid) and does not separate two bleedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the passage deals with an intervening purity (tuhr mutakhallal) between two bleedings. The core question is whether this purity separates the two bleedings into distinct hayd periods.
The purity must be less than 15 days; otherwise, it is automatically a separation.
2
Distinguish the three scenarios
The text divides the length of the intervening purity into three categories: less than 3 days, 3 to less than 15 days, and 15 days or more. Note the consensus on the first and third, and the dispute on the second.
The second scenario is the focus of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify that Abu Yusuf and the later opinion of Abu Hanifa hold that any purity less than 15 days does not separate, even if it is 3 days or more. Understand the opposing view (earlier or alternative) that might have allowed separation for 3+ days.
The author explicitly refutes the misconception that 'or more' caps at ten days.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Work through the example given: a woman sees 1 day of blood, then 14 days of purity, then 1 day of blood. According to the mufta bihi, the entire 16-day period is treated as one continuous bleeding: the first 10 days are hayd, the rest istihada.
This illustrates that the intervening 14-day purity does not separate.
5
Understand the permissibility of hayd beginning/ending with purity
The passage also explains that according to Abu Yusuf, hayd can begin and end with a day of purity, provided there is blood before and after those pure days. This is a specific application of the general rule.
This further reinforces that the purity is considered part of the hayd period.

واعلم أنَّ الطَّهِّرَ الذي يكون أقل من خمسة عشر ) إذا تخلل بين الدمين : فإن كان أقل من ثلاثة أيام لا يفصل بينهما ، بل هو كالدم المتوالي إجماعاً. وإن كان ثلاثة أيام أو أكثر"، فعند أبي يوسف ، وهو قول أبي حنيفةً ه آخراً لا يفصل ، وإن كان أكثر من عشرة أيام) فيجوز ) بداية الحيض وختمُهُ بالطُّهر على هذا القول فقط (٢٢). فإن قلت : عدم الفصل فيما إذا كان أكثر من عشرة أيضاً يفهم من إطلاق قوله : «أو أكثر» ؛ فلا حاجة إلى ذكره. قلت : ذكره تفصيلاً ورفعاً لتوهّم أنّ المراد به أكثر من ثلاثة فقط، وصورته: أن ترى امرأة دماً وأربعة عشر طهراً، ثمّ يوماً ،دماً ، ففي هذه الصورة وكذا في الصورة السابقة يعد الكـل دماً متوالياً فتجعل العشرة أو ما نقص منها حيضاً، وما زاد عليها استحاضة.
[١]قوله : فيجوز ؛ يعني لَمَّا كان الطهر الناقص عن خمسة عشر غير فاصل مطلقاً من دون تقييد بما قيَّد به غيره على ما سيأتي تفصيله فيجوز عنده ابتداء الحيض وختمه بالطهر؛ بأن يكون أوّل يوم منه وآخر يوم منه طهراً في حكم الحيض، وهذا إذا كان قبل البداية وبعد الختم دم في حكم الطهر.
ومثاله على ما في «العناية»: «امرأةُ عادتها في أوّل كل شهر خمسة أيام، رأت قبل خمستها يوماً دماً ، ثمّ طهرت أول يوم من خمستها ، ثم رأت ثلاثة دماً ، ثم طهرت إلى آخر يوم من خمستها ، ثم استمرَّ بها الدم فحيضها عند أبي يوسف له خمسة، وإن كان بدؤه وختمه بالطهر ؛ لوجود الدم قبله وبعده» فيجوز بدايته به إذا كان قبله فقط، ولا يختم به، ويجوزُ ختمه . به فقط إذا كان بعده دماً لا قبله.
Know that the purity that is less than fifteen [days] if it intervenes between two bleedings: if it is less than three days, it does not separate them, rather it is like continuous blood by consensus. If it is three days or more, then according to Abu Yusuf, and it is the later opinion of Abu Hanifa, it does not separate, even if it is more than ten days. So it is permissible for the beginning and end of menstruation to be with purity on this opinion only. If you say: Non-separation in the case of more than ten is also understood from the general statement 'or more'; so there is no need to mention it. I say: He mentioned it in detail to remove the misconception that it means only more than three. Its scenario: a woman sees blood and fourteen days of purity, then one day of blood. In this scenario and in the previous scenario, all is counted as continuous blood, so ten or whatever is less than it is taken as menstruation, and what exceeds it is istihada.
[1] His statement: 'it is permissible' means: since the purity that falls short of fifteen is absolutely non-separating without the restriction that others impose, as will be detailed later, so according to him it is permissible for menstruation to begin and end with purity; that is, its first and last day are purity in the ruling of menstruation, provided that before the beginning and after the end there is blood in the ruling of purity.
Its example according to al-'Inaya: 'A woman whose habit is five days at the beginning of each month; she saw one day of blood before her five days, then she became pure on the first day of her five days, then she saw three days of blood, then she became pure until the last day of her five days, then the blood continued. So according to Abu Yusuf, her menstruation is five days, even though its beginning and end are with purity, because there is blood before and after it.' So it is permissible for it to begin with purity if there is only blood before it, and not to end with it, and it is permissible for it to end with purity only if there is blood after it and not before.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses the ruling on an intervening period of purity (tahr mutakhallal) that occurs between two episodes of bleeding in the context of menstruation (hayd). The passage is a commentary expanding on a matn statement. The author begins by establishing a general principle: any period of purity that is less than fifteen days does not separate two bleedings; instead, it is treated as one continuous period of bleeding. This is based on the consensus that the minimum interval between two menstrual cycles is fifteen days. The text then details three scenarios based on the length of the intervening purity:

1. Less than three days: Unanimously, it does not separate. The entire duration is considered one continuous bleeding.
2. Three days or more: According to Abu Yusuf and the later opinion of Abu Hanifa, it does not separate, even if the purity extends beyond ten days (as long as it is less than fifteen). This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3. If the purity is exactly fifteen days or more, it is a valid separation, and the two bleedings are considered distinct menstrual cycles.

The passage then addresses a potential objection: if 'or more' already includes more than ten, why was it explicitly mentioned? The response clarifies that the mention is to remove the misconception that 'more' means only more than three, not more than ten. The example given is a woman who sees one day of blood, fourteen days of purity, then one day of blood. In this case, all sixteen days are considered one continuous event: the first ten days constitute hayd (since the maximum hayd is ten days), and the remaining six are istihada (non-menstrual bleeding).

The latter part of the passage discusses a specific application: the permissibility of hayd beginning and ending with purity according to Abu Yusuf. This occurs when a woman has a habit of five days at the start of each month, but she sees one day of blood before her habitual days, then purity on the first day of her habit, then three days of blood, then purity until the last day of her habit, then continuous bleeding thereafter. According to Abu Yusuf, her hayd is still the entire five-day habitual period, even though its first and last days are pure, because there is blood before and after these pure days. The conditions are that the purity at the beginning must be preceded by blood, and the purity at the end must be followed by blood.

Key Terms
الطهر المتخلل (al-tuhr al-mutakhallal): The period of purity (absence of bleeding) that occurs between two episodes of bleeding.
الفصل (al-fasl): The legal separation of two bleedings by a valid period of purity that makes them two distinct menstrual cycles.
الطهر الفاسد (al-tuhr al-fasid): A period of purity that is legally invalid for separation because it is less than 15 days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman sees blood for one day, then is pure for three days, then sees blood again, how is this treated according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) The three days of purity separate the bleedings into two distinct hayd periods.
B) The entire duration is treated as one continuous bleeding; the first 10 days are hayd, and any excess is istihada.
C) The second bleeding is considered istihada because the purity is less than 15 days.
D) The woman should count each bleeding separately according to her habit.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, only a full 15-day purity separates two menstrual bleedings; anything less is treated as one continuous bleeding.

Taharah — Purification

Abu Yusuf's View on Hayd Beginning/Ending with Purity and Fatwa on Ease
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hayd and purity with fatwa preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's view on hayd beginning/ending with purity, explain its basis in the principle of non-separating tahr, and identify why it is the mufta bihi due to ease.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf: Purity less than 15 days surrounded by blood counts as part of hayd — ease guides fatwa.

In this passage, we explore an intra-Hanafi dispute: can a woman's menstrual period begin or end with days of purity? Abu Yusuf says yes, provided blood surrounds the purity. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, requiring stricter conditions. The later mashayikh adopted Abu Yusuf's view for fatwa due to ease, supported by hadiths. Understanding this khilaf and the tarjih based on taysir is essential for applying the Hanafi school's operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Determine the exact issue: whether the first and last days of hayd can be days of purity (tahr) rather than blood.
The dispute relates to counting tahr as part of the menstrual flow.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that hayd can begin and end with purity, provided blood is present both before and after the tahr period.
The key condition is that the tahr must be surrounded by blood from both sides.
3
Understand the proof
The basis is the Hanafi principle that a tahr of less than 15 days does not separate between two bleedings. Thus, the tahr is considered part of the continuous blood period. Istihsan (juristic preference) based on ease also supports this view, as per hadiths on making things easy.
The hadiths 'Make things easy, not difficult' and 'Religion is ease' are cited.
4
Contrast with Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani requires additional conditions (e.g., that the first and last days are blood, or that the tahr does not exceed certain limits), making the ruling more restrictive and harder to apply.
The passage notes that Muhammad's view has 'conditions and details' that are difficult for women to remember.
5
Trace the tarjih
The later mashayikh (e.g., in al-Muhit, al-Sirajiyyah, al-Zuhayriyyah) gave fatwa on Abu Yusuf's view because of ease (taysir) for both the mufti and the mustafti. This makes Abu Yusuf's view the mufta bihi.
The tarjih is based on the principle that when there is ikhtilaf, the easier position is preferred for fatwa, as long as it is sound.
