وحلَّ وَطْهُ مَن قطعَ دَمُها لاكثر الحيض، أو النفاس قبل الغُسْلِ دون وَطْءِ مَن قُطِعَ لاقل منه ) : أي لأقل من الأكثر، وهو أن ينقطع الحيض لأقل من عشرة، والنفاس لأقل من أربعين، إلا إذا مضى عليها وقت يسعُ الغُسْلَ والتَّحريمة)، فحينئذ يحلُّ وَطؤها، وإن لم تغتسل إقامة للوقت الذي يُتَمَكنُ فيه من الاغتسال مقام حقيقة الاغتسال في حق جل الوطء).
(۱) قوله : وحل وطء من قطع... الخ ; قال الشارح فصيح الدين الهروي: أي حل للزوج وطء زوجته الحائض والنفساء، وكذا للمولى وطء أمته الحائض أو النفساء إذا انقطع دمها لأكثر; أي لمضي أكثر مدة الحيض إن كانت حائضاً أو النفاس إن كانت نفساء.
ويحتمل أن يكون اللام بمعنى على، وعلى كلا التقديرين هو متعلق «بقطع»، ويحتمل أن يتعلّق «بحل»، وانقطاع الدم ليس بشرط، حتى لو لم ينقطع يكون الحكم كذلك، فإن الزيادة تكون استحاضة، إلا أنه خرج مخرج العادة، أو لتناسب ما سيأتي من قوله: «دون من قطع لأقل منه». وقال البرجندي: السلام لام التاريخ، كما في كتبتُ لثلاث خلون; أي بعد ثلاث. كذا في «الصحاح»، ويحتمل أن يكون بمعنى «في»، ويكون حالا من الدم. [٢]قوله : إلا إذا مضى; لأنّ الصلاة حينئذ صارت دينا في ذمتها، فصارت طاهرة
(۱) توضيح هذه المسألة إذا انقطع دم الحائض لأقل من عشرة وكان لتمام عادتها، فإنه لا يحل وطؤها إلا بعد الاغتسال أو التيمم بشرطه; لأنه صارت طاهرة حقيقة أو بعد أن تصير الصلاة دينا في ذمتها; وذلك بأن ينقطع ويمضي عليها أدنى وقت صلاة من آخره، وهو قدر ما يسع الغسل واللبس والتحريمة سواء كان الانقطاع قبل الوقت أو في أوله أو قبيل آخره. فإذا انقطع قبل الظهر مثلاً أو في أول وقته لا يحل وطؤها حتى يدخل وقت العصر; لأنها لما مضى عليها من آخر الوقت ذلك القدر صارت الصلاة دينا في ذمتها; لأن المعتبر في الوجوب آخر الوقت، وإذا صارت الصلاة ديناً في ذمتها صارت طاهرة حكماً; لأنها لا تجب في الذمة إلا بعد الحكم عليها بالطهارة، وإنما حل وطؤها بعد الحكم عليها بالطهارة بصيرورة الصلاة دينا في ذمتها; لأنها صارت كالجنب وخرجت من الحيض حكما، وبه يعلم أنه لا يجوز لها قراءة القرآن. ينظر: (رد المحتار» (١ : ١٩٦).
And the intercourse of one whose blood ceases for more than the maximum of menses or lochia is permissible before ghusl, unlike the intercourse of one who ceases for less than the maximum; i.e., less than the maximum, which is that menses ceases at less than ten days, and lochia at less than forty, unless time has passed sufficient for ghusl and the opening takbir, then her intercourse becomes permissible even if she has not performed ghusl, by making the time in which she is able to perform ghusl stand in place of the actual ghusl regarding permissibility of intercourse. (1) His statement: 'And the intercourse of one who ceases...' etc.; the commentator Faseeh al-Din al-Harawi said: It is permissible for the husband to have intercourse with his menstruating or postpartum wife, and likewise for the master to have intercourse with his slave-girl who is menstruating or postpartum, when her blood ceases for more (than the maximum); i.e., due to the passage of more than the maximum duration of menses if she is menstruating, or lochia if she is postpartum. And it is possible that the 'lam' is in the sense of 'upon' (meaning 'after'), and in both interpretations it is attached to 'ceases', and it is possible that it is attached to 'permissible' [with the meaning of 'for'] but the cessation of blood is not a condition, such that even if it does not cease, the ruling is the same, for the increase would be istihada (irregular bleeding), but it appears as custom or for harmony with what will come of his statement: 'unlike one who ceases for less than the maximum.' And al-Barjandi said: 'al-salam' is 'lam' of date, as in 'I wrote for three days past'; i.e., after three. Thus in 'al-Sihah', and it is possible it is in the sense of 'during', being a state of the blood. [2] His statement: 'unless time has passed'; because the prayer at that time becomes a debt upon her responsibility, so she becomes pure. (1) Clarification of this issue: If the blood of a menstruating woman ceases at less than ten days and it is completion of her habit, then her intercourse is not permissible except after ghusl or tayammum with its conditions, because she becomes truly pure, or after the prayer becomes a debt upon her responsibility; that is, by cessation and the passage of the minimum prayer time from its end, which is the time sufficient for ghusl, dressing, and the opening takbir, whether the cessation was before the time, at its beginning, or shortly before its end. So if it ceases before Dhuhr for example or at its beginning, her intercourse is not permissible until the time of Asr enters; because when that amount from the end of the time has passed, the prayer becomes a debt upon her responsibility; for the consideration in obligation is the end of the time, and when the prayer becomes a debt upon her responsibility, she becomes pure in ruling; because it is not obligatory upon the responsibility except after ruling her to be pure. Her intercourse is only permissible after ruling her to be pure by the prayer becoming a debt upon her responsibility; because she becomes like a junub and exits from menses in ruling, and from this it is known that she is not permitted to recite the Quran. See: Radd al-Muhtar (1:196).
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage addresses a crucial point in Hanafi fiqh regarding when a husband may have intercourse with his wife after her menstruation or postpartum bleeding has stopped, before she performs ghusl. The matn states that if the bleeding stops after the maximum period (10 days for menses, 40 for lochia), intercourse is permissible even without ghusl. If it stops before the maximum, it is not permissible unless time sufficient for ghusl and the opening takbir (i.e., one prayer time) has passed, in which case it becomes permissible even without actual ghusl. The commentary explains the reasoning: when the bleeding stops before the maximum, the woman is not yet completely pure; she remains in the ruling of menstruation until she performs ghusl. However, if she delays ghusl until a full prayer time (like from the end of Dhuhr to the beginning of Asr) passes without her praying, the prayer becomes a debt (dayn) upon her, meaning she is obligated to make it up. This indicates that, according to Hanafi law, she is considered pure in ruling (hukman) at that point, because obligation cannot be imposed on someone in a state of impurity. Therefore, intercourse is permissible, as she is now like a junub (who can have intercourse) and has exited the ruling of menstruation. The commentary also clarifies that this applies whether the bleeding stops during a prayer time or not, as long as enough time for ghusl and takbir from the end of the time has passed.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that starts the prayer, used here to measure the minimum time for ghusl and prayer initiation.
دين في الذمة (dayn fi al-dhimmah): A debt upon one's responsibility; here referring to the missed prayer that must be made up (qada'), indicating the woman is considered pure.
استحاضة (istihadah): Irregular bleeding that is not menstrual or postpartum; a woman in istihadah is legally pure and can pray and have intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, if a woman's menses stops on the 8th day but she does not perform ghusl, when is intercourse permissible?
A) Immediately, because bleeding has stopped.
B) Only after she performs ghusl or tayammum.
C) After the passage of time sufficient for ghusl and takbir from the end of a prayer time.
D) After she has prayed one complete prayer.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse is permissible without ghusl if bleeding stops after the maximum, or if before the maximum, after the passage of one prayer time from its end.

Intercourse After Hayd and Nifas: When Is It Permissible?
Ruling on when intercourse is permissible after hayd/nifas bleeding stops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when intercourse is permissible after menstruation (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas) stops, and explain the concept of legal purity (hukman) based on the passage of time sufficient for ghusl and takbir.

Core Idea
If bleeding stops after the maximum (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas), intercourse is halal even without ghusl; if it stops before, time enough for ghusl and takbir must pass.

This lesson tackles a common practical question: when exactly is it permissible to resume marital relations after a woman's period or postpartum bleeding ends? The Hanafi school distinguishes between two scenarios depending on whether the bleeding stops after the maximum duration or before. The ruling also introduces a unique legal concept: the sufficiency of a time window for ghusl, even if actual ghusl hasn't been performed, based on the idea that prayer becomes a debt on her, indicating legal purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the opening sentence: Bleeding stops 'for the maximum' (li-akthar) vs 'for less than that' (li-aqall). Understand that 'maximum' for hayd is 10 days, for nifas is 40 days in the Hanafi school.
The text uses 'la' as 'for' indicating the time of cessation.
2
Analyze the ruling for each scenario
For bleeding stopping after the maximum: intercourse is halal immediately, even without ghusl. For bleeding stopping before the maximum: intercourse is not halal until a time sufficient for ghusl and takbir passes (i.e., enough time to perform ghusl, put on clothes, and say the opening takbir). This time is measured from the end of the prayer time.
The ruling depends on whether the woman is considered pure (tahirah) in reality or legally (hukman).
3
Understand the proof (talil)
The proof lies in the concept of legal purity. When a time sufficient for ghusl passes, the prayer of that time becomes a debt (dayn) on her. This indicates that she is legally pure, because prayer is only obligatory on a pure person. This legal purity allows intercourse even without actual ghusl.
The time is considered equivalent to actual ghusl for the purpose of permitting intercourse.
4
Apply the time calculation
The sufficient time is the minimum period needed for ghusl, dressing, and saying the opening takbir (approx. a short while). It is measured from the end of the prayer time (e.g., if bleeding stops before Zuhr, she must wait until just before Asr for that time to pass). The commentary clarifies that cessation alone is not the condition; it is the passing of that time.
This shows that legal purity is established by the obligation of prayer, not by actual cleanliness.

And it is halal to have intercourse with her whose blood stops for the maximum of menstruation or postpartum bleeding before ghusl, without intercourse with her who stops for less than that, unless a time passes sufficient for ghusl and takbir. When prayer becomes a debt upon her, she becomes pure legally, because it is not obligated upon her except after ruling her pure. Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on when a husband may have intercourse with his wife after her menstrual or postpartum bleeding stops. The author begins by stating two scenarios: first, if the bleeding stops after the maximum duration of hayd (ten days) or nifas (forty days), then intercourse is permissible even before she performs ghusl. Second, if the bleeding stops before the maximum, then intercourse is not permissible unless a period of time passes that is sufficient for her to perform ghusl and say the takbir for prayer (i.e., enough time for one rakʿah after the start of the prayer time). The commentator explains that the time in which she is capable of performing ghusl is considered equivalent to actual ghusl for the purpose of allowing intercourse. The proof is that when such a time passes, prayer becomes a debt (dayn) upon her, indicating she has become pure in legal ruling (hukman). Thus, she is like a person in major impurity (junub) and has exited the state of hayd legally. This also implies she cannot recite Quran during that time. The commentary also clarifies linguistic nuances and emphasizes that cessation of blood is not a condition for the ruling; even if bleeding continues beyond the maximum, the same applies because excess beyond maximum is istihadah.

Key Terms
أكثر الحيض (akthar al-hayd): The maximum duration of menstruation, which in the Hanafi school is ten days.
أقل الحيض (aqall al-hayd): The minimum duration of menstruation, which in the Hanafi school is three days.
وقت يسع الغسل والتحريمة (waqt yasi' al-ghusl wa al-tahrimah): A period of time sufficient for performing ghusl and saying the opening takbir for prayer, i.e., enough time for one rakʿah.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after hayd or nifas is permissible either immediately if bleeding stops after the maximum duration, or after the passage of a time sufficient for ghusl and takbir if it stops before the maximum.

Cessation of Menses Before Habit Ends
Ruling for cessation before habit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling when a woman's bleeding stops before her habit days are complete, and explain the rationale based on predominant return of blood.

Core Idea
If bleeding stops before habit ends, she remains in hayd until habit days pass.

A common scenario in menstrual fiqh is when a woman's bleeding stops earlier than her usual number of days. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling that balances precaution and practical necessity. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains how such a woman must handle ghusl, prayers, and marital relations. We will unpack the legal reasoning and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes cessation before habit (duna al-ādah) and cessation at or after habit, or for a beginner. Determine which scenario is being discussed.
This lesson focuses on cessation before habit.
2
State the ruling for ghusl and prayer
When bleeding stops before habit, she must delay ghusl until the end of the prayer time. If she fears missing the prayer, she may perform ghusl and pray, but she is not considered pure.
The delay is wajib, not optional.
3
Determine the ruling for marital relations
Even if she performs ghusl and prays, intercourse remains impermissible until the full habit days have passed.
This is due to the strong probability that bleeding will return.
4
Understand the rationale (ʿillah)
The basis is that return of blood within the habit is predominant (ghālib), and deviation is rare (nādir). Therefore, she is treated as still menstruating until habit ends.
This is a dalīl ʿaqlī (rational proof) based on custom and probability.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete example
For a woman with a 7-day habit who stops on day 5: she delays ghusl until the end of each prayer time, and if she prays due to fear of missing, she must still wait until day 7 for intercourse.
After day 7, if no blood returns, she must make up any prayers she performed during days 5-7? Actually, the text says if it does not return, those prayers are valid? The passage indicates if it returns, intervening purity is non-intervening; if not, she is pure and prayers are valid. But the ruling on making up is for the case of cessation at habit or beginner. So not needed here.

واعلم أنه إذا انقطع الدَّمُ لأقل من عشرة أيام بعد ما مَضَى ثلاثة أيام أو فإن كان الانقطاع فيما دون العادة " يجب " أن تؤخِّرَ الغُسل إلى آخر وقت الصلاة، فإذا خافت فوت الصَّلاة اغتسلت وصلت ، والمراد آخر الوقت المستحب دون وقتِ الكراهة. وإن كان الانقطاع على رأس عادتها ، أو أكثر، أو كانت مبتدأة حكماً، فإن بالاغتسال يحكم بطهارتها، ويوجدان وقت التحريمة يجب القضاء. [١] قوله : بعد ما مضى؛ ما مصدرية ; أي بعد مضي ثلاثة أو أكثر مثلاً انقطع لسبعة أيام أو خمسة أيام. [٢]قوله : فيما دون العادة ; إذا كانت معتادة بأن كانت عادته أن تحيض في كلّ شهر سبعة أيام فانقطع دمها في شهر لستة أيام. [٣]قوله : يجب ; يعني لا تبادر إلى الغُسلِ وأداء الصلاة ونحوها، بل تنتظر إلى آخر وقت الصلاة ; لأن عود الدم مظنون لبقاء زمان العادة، والتخلّف عن العادة أمر نادر ، فإن عاد دمها فهي. حائضة كما كانت ، وما تخلل من الطهر غير فاصل. وإن لم يعد وخافت فوت الصلاة ونقصانها بذهاب الوقت اغتسلت وأدت الصلاة احتياطاً، لكن لا يحلّ الوطء في هذه الصورة: أي ما انقطع الدم لدون عادتها ، وإن اغتسلت إلا بعد مضي أيام العادة ; لأنَّ العودَ في العادة غالب، فكان الاحتياط في الاجتناب. كذا في «الهداية». [٤] قوله : دون وقت الكراهة ; نص عليه محمد له في «الأصل» حيث قال : «إذا انقطع الدم في وقت العشاء تؤخّر إلى وقت يمكنها أن تغتسل فيه وتصلّي قبل انتصاف الليل، وما بعد نصف الليل مكروه». [0] قوله : أو كانت مبتدأة ; بصيغة المجهول، هي التي ابتدأ بلوغها بالحيض، ولم تستقر عادتها.
And know that if the stops in less than ten days after three or more days have passed, then if the cessation is within [i.e., before] her habit, she must delay ghusl to the end of the prayer time. If she fears missing the prayer, she performs ghusl and prays. The intended [time] is the end of the preferred time, not the disliked time. If the cessation is at the end of her habit, or more, or she is a beginner legally, then by ghusl she is ruled pure, and at the time of the opening takbir, she must make up [the prayer]. [1] Statement: 'after three days have passed'; ma is masdariyya; i.e., after three or more pass, for example it stops for seven days or five days. [2] Statement: 'within [i.e., before] the habit'; when she is a habitual one, her habit being that she menstruates every month for seven days, but her blood stops in a month for six days. [3] Statement: 'must'; meaning she should not hasten to ghusl and performing prayer and the like, but wait until the end of the prayer time, because return of blood is expected due to the remaining time of the habit, and deviation from habit is rare. If her blood returns, she is menstruating as before, and the intervening purity is not intervening. If it does not return and she fears missing the prayer or its deficiency with the passing of time, she performs ghusl and prays as a precaution, but intercourse is not permissible in this case: i.e., that which stops before her habit, even if she performs ghusl, except after the passing of the habit days, because return during the habit is predominant, so precaution is in avoidance. Thus in al-Hidayah. [4] Statement: 'without the disliked time'; this is stated by Muhammad in al-Asl where he said: 'If blood stops at the time of Isha, she delays until a time when she can perform ghusl and pray before midnight; after midnight is disliked.' [0] Statement: 'or she is a beginner'; in the passive voice, she is one whose puberty began with menstruation and her habit has not been established.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for a woman whose menstrual bleeding stops before completing ten days, assuming at least three days have passed. The author distinguishes based on whether the cessation is before her usual habit (ādah) or at/after it. If the cessation is before her habit, she should not hasten to perform ghusl and pray; rather, she must wait until the end of the prayer time to see if bleeding returns, because it is likely to return. If she fears missing the prayer entirely, she may perform ghusl and pray, but intercourse is not permissible even after ghusl until after the full habit days have passed. This is precaution (ihtiyat) because the return of blood within the habit is predominant. If the cessation occurs at the conclusion of her habit, or she is a beginner (mubtada'ah), then once she performs ghusl, she becomes pure and must make up missed prayers from the time of purity. The commentary also clarifies that the end of the preferred time is meant, not the time of karahat, and cites Imam Muhammad from al-Asl regarding the case of Isha.

Key Terms
العادة (al-ādah): The usual number of days a woman menstruates each month, established by habit.
المبتدأة (al-mubtada'ah): A woman who has just reached puberty and experienced her first menstruation, so she has no established habit.
الانقطاع دون العادة (al-inqitā' dūna al-ādah): Cessation of bleeding before the end of her usual habit days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman with a 7-day habit stops bleeding on day 5. When is intercourse permissible?
A) Immediately after stopping, if she performs ghusl
B) Only after completing 7 days (habit), regardless of ghusl
C) Exactly on day 6 regardless
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Cessation before habit does not end hayd; she must wait until habit days complete for full purity, and intercourse remains forbidden.
